# Night Shift Changelog

Newest first. One entry per cycle. The loop appends here; you read it over coffee.

## 2026-06-29T112442Z — PASS — post-platform-default
- Pages: /partnerships/new (Post a Partnership form), /partnerships/seeking/new (Post a Seeking Listing form), /partnerships/[id] + /partnerships/seeking/[id] (contact display — no code change, regression-checked)
- What: **Posting a partnership or seeking listing now defaults to on-platform messaging instead of exposing the poster's email.** Both post forms gain "Message through ClubHanger (default)" as the first "Preferred Contact Method" option, ahead of the existing "Email only / Phone only / Email or phone" choices, and the server actions (`createPartnership`, `createSeekerListing`) now fall back to `contact_method='platform'` instead of `'email'` when nothing is submitted. The misleading "Not shown publicly" helper text under the email field — which was wrong for the `email`/`both` cases — is corrected to "Only shared when you select email contact above." Net effect: a new poster who doesn't actively choose email keeps their address private and routes buyers through the in-app Message thread, which both protects privacy and keeps engagement on-site. Existing listings are untouched (rows with `contact_method='email'` still render "Send Email"); `ContactButtons`/`SeekerContactBar` already suppress email/phone links and show only the Message button for `platform`, so no component change was needed.
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — removes a privacy-exposing decision from the posting flow and makes the privacy-preserving, engagement-keeping choice the default. Rotation: last PASS was Pillar 3 (ifr-badge-browse-cards), before that Pillar 1 (aircraft-contact-phone) then Pillar 3 (avionics-ifr-land); Pillar 1 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth. No schema change, no DB migration, additive only. (This branch's PM+Eng steps were prepared by a prior interrupted cycle as a working-tree diff + spec; this cycle verified the downstream `platform` handling, committed, built, QA'd, and landed it — same pickup pattern as aircraft-contact-phone.)
- Spec: nightshift/specs/2026-06-29T112442Z-post-platform-default.md
- Verdict: PASS — `rm -rf .next && npx next build` exit 0 (✓ compiled in 27.7s, 370/370 static pages); `tsc --noEmit` exit 0 (0 type errors). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start` on port 3430) via `qa-smoke.mjs` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on `/partnerships/new` + `/partnerships/seeking/new` + one partnership detail + one seeker detail: 8/8 checks pass (HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow). Visual cycle — read screenshots: both post forms render cleanly at both viewports with no overflow. The changed select lives inside the collapsed "More details" section so it isn't in the default smoke screenshots; a targeted Playwright render with that section expanded confirmed both forms list `["Message through ClubHanger (default)","Email only","Phone only","Email or phone"]` as the contact-method options and that the corrected helper text is present. Env note: the QA browser had to be installed to a writable local path (`PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSERS_PATH=/tmp/pw`) — the project's playwright-core pins chromium-headless-shell **1228** but the image's read-only `/ms-playwright` only ships **1223**; `/ms-playwright` is root-owned and not writable by the `night` user, so the matching browser cannot be installed system-wide. Future cycles in this environment will hit the same gap until the image bakes in 1228 (or `/ms-playwright` is made writable).
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/post-platform-default/
- Next: (1) Pillar 1 — conditionally hide/show the email input based on the selected contact method (JS state — when "Message through ClubHanger" is selected, the email field is irrelevant and can collapse), the natural follow-on to this slice; or "Paste & prefill the whole form" (extend AI-draft to map all fields from a pasted blob/URL) remains the biggest open P1 posting slice; or the user-posted aircraft detail page ([P2][want] — user-posted listings with source_url=null link to a # dead end, needs an internal /aircraft/[id] route). (2) Pillar 3 — "Market position + days-on-market" context on aircraft browse cards (comp-count/median is only on the detail page today). (3) Pillar 2 — "Continue with Google" OAuth remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.

## 2026-06-29T105848Z — PASS — ifr-badge-browse-cards
- Pages: /aircraft (browse cards — avionics badge row)
- What: **Aircraft browse cards now show a synthesized IFR verdict badge for glass-panel and capable-IFR aircraft instead of raw individual avionics chips.** Before, a Cirrus SR22 with G1000+WAAS+autopilot showed "Glass panel" + "ADS-B Out" as two separate chips — useful, but not a buyer answer. Now it shows "Full IFR setup" (emerald) or "IFR-capable: WAAS GPS + autopilot" (sky-blue) as a single synthesized verdict chip, so a buyer scanning the browse list gets an immediate IFR suitability read without clicking into the detail page. Aircraft without IFR-grade avionics keep their individual capability chips unchanged. Four IFR verdict badges were confirmed on the live browse page; 20 individual avionics chips remain on non-qualifying aircraft.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — surfaces the synthesized IFR verdict (already live on aircraft detail pages and partnership detail pages) directly into the browse experience. Reuses `computeIfrSuitability` from `src/lib/avionicsClassify.ts` (12 unit tests, already in codebase) — no new logic, no DB changes, no schema changes. Rotation: last PASS was Pillar 1 (aircraft-contact-phone); Pillar 3 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.

On the detail page, the phone number renders as a `tel:` link only for user-posted listings that have a phone set — self-suppresses for scraped listings and for user-posted listings without one. Closes the parity gap vs. the partnership post form which has always collected contact_phone. No schema change: the `contact_phone text` column and `createAircraftListing` action already accepted the field; this cycle surfaces it in the UI.

## 2026-06-29T092536Z — PASS — past-listings-relist
- Pages: /listings (My Listings management page — new "Past listings" collapsible section)
- What: **Sellers can now see their closed and sold listings on the /listings management page, and relist them in one click.** Before, once a seller marked their aircraft as sold, closed their partnership, or deactivated a seeking listing, those listings disappeared from /listings with no way to recover them without re-posting from scratch. Now a collapsible "Past listings (N) — sold & closed" section appears at the bottom of /listings showing all three types. Each past listing shows a "Sold" or "Closed" status badge, the title, key details, a "View →" link, and a "Relist" button. Clicking "Relist" shows a confirm dialog, then flips the listing's status back to active (and resets `posted_at` to now for partnerships so they re-appear at the top of date-sorted browse feeds). The listing moves from Past listings back to the active section on the same page.
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — completes the listing lifecycle management loop on /listings. The `listings-deactivate-action` cycle (previous cycle in this drain) added the deactivate path; this cycle closes the loop by adding the relist/restore path. A seller whose plane briefly sold, whose partnership spot re-opened, or who wants to re-seek after a break can now act in one click without re-entering all their listing data. The StatusBadge component was also updated to show distinct "Sold" and "Closed" labels (slate styling) instead of the previous catch-all "Pending" for non-active states. No schema changes: status columns already exist on all three tables. Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 3 (avionics-ifr-summary), so Pillar 1 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260629T092536Z-past-listings-relist.md
- Verdict: PASS — `npx next build` compiled successfully (✓ 29.0s); `tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0, 0 type errors). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start` on port 3300) via qa-smoke at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on `/listings`: HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow, exit 0. Visual cycle — screenshots show the auth page rendered correctly (the /listings auth-gate redirect is working as expected; the management content is auth-gated so only logged-in users see it — the code path is verified by the clean build and type check). Key code verified by inspection: `relistListing` server action checks `poster_id = user.id` on all three table paths (same defense-in-depth pattern as `deactivateListing`); `RelistListingButton` uses `useTransition` for pending state; `pastCount` drives the Past section visibility (no section when no past listings); StatusBadge now renders distinct styling for 'sold', 'closed', 'active', and 'pending' states.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/past-listings-relist/

## 2026-06-29T091132Z — PASS — avionics-ifr-summary
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id] (aircraft for-sale detail page — Avionics & Panel section + Deal Score tally)
- What: **Aircraft listing pages now synthesize the extracted avionics list into a plain-English IFR suitability verdict at the top of the Avionics & Panel section.** Before, the panel showed capability chips (Glass panel, ADS-B Out, Autopilot, WAAS GPS) and a raw equipment list, but gave no synthesized read on what those chips mean for IFR capability. Now a colored verdict badge appears above the chips — "Full IFR touring setup" (emerald, when glass + WAAS + autopilot are all present), "IFR-capable: WAAS GPS + autopilot" (sky blue), "Glass panel with autopilot" (sky blue), and so on down to "ADS-B compliant" (slate) for aircraft with compliance hardware but no nav suite. An explanatory sentence follows the badge. For full/capable IFR tiers, the same verdict also appears as a positive row in the "How this stacks up" Deal Score tally — so a buyer sees the IFR capability signal in the main verdict even before scrolling to the Avionics section. Self-suppresses when no capability chips were detected (raw equipment list only, no recognizable glass/GPS/autopilot patterns) — no fabricated IFR claim.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — turns the raw avionics classifier output into a synthesized buyer read that no other listing site offers. Controller and Barnstormers print the avionics list verbatim; ClubHanger now answers the question every IFR buyer actually asks: "Can I file IFR in this aircraft, and is it a capable setup?" Honesty-gated: only fires on detected caps (never asserts IFR-capable from an empty list), and the badge text is descriptive (what was found) rather than a guarantee. Reuses the already-computed `classifyAvionics()` output on the page — no new DB queries, no schema changes, no new library files. Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 1 (listings-deactivate-action), so Pillar 3 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260629T091132Z-avionics-ifr-summary.md

Verify WAAS GPS details with the owner for precision approaches." — correct `capable` tier verdict, clean layout at 1280px and 375px with no overflow. ## 2026-06-29T090346Z — PASS — listings-deactivate-action
- Pages: /listings (My Listings management page)
- What: **Listing owners can now close or deactivate their own listings directly from the /listings management page.** Before, the page only had a "View →" link — a seller whose plane sold or a partnership owner whose spots filled had no way to remove their listing from ClubHanger without contacting support. Now each aircraft row has a "Mark as sold" button, each partnership row has a "Close listing" button, and each seeker row has a "Deactivate" button. Each uses a `window.confirm` dialog to prevent accidental clicks, shows a "Closing…" pending state, and disappears the listing from /listings once the action completes. The server action (`deactivateListing`) is owner-gated: it verifies `poster_id = user.id` in the DB query (defense-in-depth on top of the existing RLS `update using (auth.uid() = poster_id)` policies that already protect all three tables).
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — closes the listing-management gap on /listings, explicitly called out in the previous cycle's "Next:" note as the main remaining P1 posting slice. A post flow that has no deactivation path is incomplete — sellers need to be able to signal that a plane sold or a partnership filled. No schema changes: `status` columns already exist on all three tables (`aircraft_for_sale.status` maps to 'sold'; `partnerships.status` and `partnership_seekers.status` map to 'closed'). Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 3 (nearby-partnerships-panel), so Pillar 1 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260629T090346Z-listings-deactivate-action.md
- Verdict: PASS — `npx next build` compiled successfully (✓ 29.3s); `tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0, 0 type errors). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start` on port 3280) via qa-smoke at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on `/listings`: HTTP 200 (redirect to /auth followed cleanly), zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow, exit 0. Visual cycle — screenshots show the auth page rendered correctly (the /listings redirect is working as expected; the management buttons are auth-gated so they only appear when logged in — the code path is verified by the clean build and type check rather than a headless screenshot). Acceptance criteria verified via code inspection: `deactivateListing` checks `poster_id = user.id` on all three table paths; `DeactivateListingButton` uses `useTransition` for pending state; confirm dialogs use distinct per-type messages; the /listings page renders the correct button for each listing type. No new DB columns or queries.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/listings-deactivate-action/

## 2026-06-29T085335Z — PASS — nearby-partnerships-panel
- Pages: /partnerships/[id] (partnership detail page — sidebar)
- What: **The partnership detail sidebar now shows "Also near [AIRPORT]" — how many other active partnerships are within 100 nautical miles of this listing's home airport, with a direct link to browse them.** When viewing a Cessna 172 partnership at KPAO, a buyer now sees "19 other active partnerships within 100 nm of Palo Alto, CA → Browse all 19 nearby →" — immediately knowing whether this listing is the only option near their home field or one of many. The panel self-suppresses entirely when the airport has no other active partnerships within range (e.g., KAUS showed zero nearby, so the panel is hidden — no false promise of alternatives). The link goes to the existing `/partnerships/near/[icao]` route which already shows the same nearby listings in full.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — competitive context on the listing page that no other listing site offers. A buyer evaluating a specific partnership share now has an immediate answer to "is this my only option here, or are there others I should compare?" without leaving the page or knowing to search. Reuses the existing `NEAR_RADIUS_NM = 100` honesty constant and the `/partnerships/near/[icao]` page infrastructure already built and indexed. New `countNearbyPartnerships()` helper uses 3 narrow DB queries (airport coords, active partnership ids/home_airports, distinct airport coords for those) rather than the full `getNearbyPartnerships()` page fetch — appropriately lightweight for a sidebar widget. Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 1 (seeker-on-listings-page), so Pillar 3 is due. Pillar 2 (Google OAuth) remains human-blocked on frozen /auth.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260629T085335Z-nearby-partnerships-panel.md
- Verdict: PASS — `npx next build` compiled successfully (✓ 29.6s); `tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0, 0 type errors). ## 2026-06-29T061308Z — PASS — partnership-implied-value
- Pages: /partnerships/[id] (partnership listing detail — "How this partnership stacks up" panel)
- What: **The "How this partnership stacks up" panel on partnership detail pages now shows whether the implied full-aircraft value (buy-in × total shares) lines up with what the same make/model actually sells for on the open market.** Before, the panel only compared buy-ins against other partnership listings — it never crossed the silo to the for-sale market. Now, when a partnership has both a buy-in price and a total-shares count, the panel computes `buy_in × total_shares` and compares it to the median asking price of same make/model aircraft currently for sale on ClubHanger. On a 1/4-share Cirrus SR22 at $32,000, for example, the panel shows "Implied aircraft value looks favorable — 4 × $32,000 = $128,000 implied value, X% below the $Y median of N Cirrus SR22 aircraft for sale." When the implied value is near the for-sale median, it reads neutral with the same arithmetic. When it's above the for-sale median, it reads as "ask the owner what the buy-in includes (reserves, improvements)" — framed as a question to ask, not an accusation. The signal always shows the full math (shares × buy-in = implied total) and the source comp count so buyers know the basis, and notes that buy-ins may include reserves or other costs beyond pure aircraft equity.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — a cross-silo, honesty-gated sanity check that no other listing site offers: partnership share math fused with the for-sale market on the same platform. The implied-value concept was explicitly teed up in the `cost-per-flight-hour` CHANGELOG Next note: "a partnership-side 'implied full-aircraft value from buy-in × shares vs. for-sale family median' cross-check (honesty-gated: frame buy-in as possibly including reserves, reuse the ≥4-comp / dead-band floors)." Reuses `getFamilyAskingPrices` + `resolveMakeModelFamily` from the aircraft detail page's Estimate pipeline — no new DB columns, no new query pattern. Honesty guardrails: self-suppresses when total_shares < 2, buy_in is null, fewer than 4 for-sale comps, or make/model doesn't resolve a family via resolveMakeModelFamily; uses a ±10% dead-band (wider than aircraft comps' 5% to account for buy-in potentially including reserves/overhead beyond proportional aircraft equity); always shows the full arithmetic and comp count. New pure helper computeImpliedValueCheck (src/lib/partnershipImpliedValue.ts, 14 unit tests). Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 1 (seeker-ratings-chips), so Pillar 3 is due; Pillar 2's headline items (Google OAuth, email-only signup) remain human-blocked behind frozen /auth.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260629T061308Z-partnership-implied-value.md
- Verdict: PASS — `npx next build` + `tsc --noEmit` green (0 type errors, 0 new errors). Unit tests `node --experimental-strip-types --test src/lib/partnershipImpliedValue.test.ts` — all **14 pass** (null-gating on missing buyIn/totalShares, totalShares < 2, thin comp set; below/near/above classification; dead-band edge; even-array median; junk-price filtering). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start` on port 3201) via qa-smoke at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on three partnership listings: all 6 checks HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow, exit 0. Honesty guardrails respected: both rows REUSE the existing pure, unit-tested reads already computed on the page (`computeAnnualStatus`, `computeDamageHistory`) and inherit their self-suppression — no row appears when `annual_due` is missing/unparseable/outside the plausible annual window, or when `damage_history` wasn't extracted (we never infer "no damage" from an absent flag, never fabricate an annual status, and keep month-granular framing with "the listing states…/confirm" language). No new DB columns, queries, extraction, or composite numeric score; both inputs were already on the page. Annual-due-soon is marked neutral (a routine recurring cost, not a red flag) so it doesn't inflate the "to ask about" count. ## 2026-06-29T030110Z — PASS — engine-overhaul-timeline
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id] (Planes for Sale detail), /partnerships/[id] (Partnership detail)
- What: **The Engine Life section now tells you *when*, not just how many hours, until the next overhaul.** It takes the engine hours still left before TBO and divides them by how much this specific aircraft has actually been flown each year over its life — so a buyer sees a plain-English line like "≈ 10.5 years to overhaul at its historical pace" right under the hours-remaining bar. It only appears when the engine is still within TBO *and* we know the aircraft's flying history; if the engine is already past TBO or the hours/age aren't known, the line stays hidden (no guessing). It's clearly labelled a rough projection, since a new owner's flying rate will change the timeline.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — a genuinely new, honest synthesis that FUSES two reads already on the page (the engine's hours-to-TBO from `computeEngineLife` and the aircraft's life-average utilization from `computeAirframeUsage`) into the calendar answer a buyer actually wants ("how many years until I'm on the hook for an overhaul?"). No listing site offers this — hours-to-TBO alone can't answer it (the same 600 hrs is ~12 years for a 50 hrs/yr flyer but ~4 years for a 150 hrs/yr flyer). Honesty guardrails respected: new pure `computeOverhaulTimeline` lib self-suppresses when the engine is at/beyond TBO (the panel already surfaces that case), when utilization is unknown, or when hrs/yr ≤ 0; rounds to the half-year and floors at 0.5 so a nearly-run-out engine never reads "0 years"; framed explicitly as a rough projection off the aircraft's *historical* rate (never a guarantee), and reuses the two existing honesty-gated reads unchanged — no new DB columns, queries, or fabricated figures. node:test unit tests cover all suppression cases + the rate→years arithmetic + rounding. Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 1 (ai-prefill-faa-backfill); the one before Pillar 3 (partnership-airframe-time) — most recent was Pillar 1, so Pillar 3 is due. Pillar 2's headline items (Google OAuth, email-only signup) remain human-blocked behind the frozen `/auth`. ## 2026-06-29T023352Z — PASS — ai-prefill-faa-backfill
- Pages: /aircraft/new (Sell an Aircraft post form)
- What: **Pasting your notes into the aircraft post form now also verifies the tail number against the FAA registry.** When you use "Prefill from your notes ✨" and your text mentions an N-number but doesn't spell out the make, model, or year, the form now automatically looks that aircraft up in the FAA Aircraft Registry and fills in whatever the AI couldn't determine. So a seller who pastes almost nothing — e.g. "Selling N739WL, hangared at KAUS, $180k" — still ends up with a near-complete, registry-accurate listing in a single click, instead of a blank make/model/year. It only backfills fields the AI left empty (it never overwrites something the AI already pulled out of your notes), and if the registry has no match or is unavailable it quietly leaves the AI's draft untouched.
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — advances the BACKLOG `[P1][goal]` "Paste & prefill the whole form" item by fusing the AI draft with authoritative FAA-registry data. Friction removed: the manual second step of typing/looking up the N-number after an AI prefill that came up short on the core spec fields — one paste now yields both the AI write-up and the registry-verified make/model/year. Data-integrity guardrail *strengthened*, not weakened: backfilled values come only from the existing `/api/faa-lookup` route (never fabricated), fill only-empty so the AI's own extraction is never clobbered, and the path fails soft (registry miss/unavailable → AI draft kept, nothing invented). The "Start over" in-flight guard (`fillTokenRef`) still cancels a chained lookup so a cleared form can't be re-populated. Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 3 (partnership-airframe-time), the one before Pillar 1 (partnership-photos-survive-auth) — most recent was P3, so Pillar 1 is due. Pillar 2's headline items (Google OAuth, email-only signup) remain human-blocked behind the frozen `/auth`. This directly completes the `post-photos-survive-auth` lineage, whose changelog explicitly noted "partnership/seeker forms pass neither prop → unchanged" — the partnership form was the remaining gap (the seeker form has no photo uploader, so nothing to persist there). Data-integrity guardrail respected: persistence is the same opt-in localStorage mirror already shipped and QA'd on the aircraft form, gated on the text-draft key so no stale photos leak into a fresh listing after publish; the uploader component, upload endpoint, server action, and data model are all untouched. ## 2026-06-29T010500Z — PASS — aircraft-post-engine-type
- Pages: /aircraft/new (Sell-your-Aircraft post form), /aircraft/listing/[id] (downstream — Engine Life panel)
- What: **The "Sell your aircraft" form now captures the engine type, so a plane you post here can finally show our proprietary Engine Life & overhaul-reserve estimate on its listing page.** Until now, the Engine Life panel — "≈ X hrs / ~Y yrs to overhaul; budget ~$Z reserve", computed from SMOH + engine family — only ever appeared on *scraped* listings, because the post form collected SMOH but never the engine. So a seller who posted their own aircraft got SMOH but no engine read, and the panel silently stayed hidden. This adds an optional **Engine** field (e.g. "Lycoming IO-360", "Continental IO-550") inside the existing "More details" block, right next to SMOH, with a one-line hint explaining it powers the Engine Life estimate. The field is **optional and free-text** — it never blocks publishing — and "Prefill from your notes" (the AI draft) now also reads the engine designation out of a pasted listing blob and fills it in (omitting it when the notes don't mention one, never inventing one). The value persists to the existing `aircraft_for_sale.engine_type` column (which already drives the panel), so once a seller fills it the Engine Life analysis appears on their listing exactly like it does for scraped aircraft. The panel itself is unchanged: if the engine string doesn't match a known piston-GA TBO family, it self-suppresses (shows nothing) rather than guess.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — extends the *coverage* of an existing honest module (Engine Life / overhaul reserve) to user-posted listings, which structurally could never trigger it because the post form never collected `engine_type`. Delivered via a minimal Pillar-1 posting field (one optional input + one AI-prefill line), so it also shaves a gap in the post flow without adding a required field. Honesty guardrails respected: no new data model (column already exists), free-text + optional (no integrity/required-field regression), the AI prefill omits engine when absent (never fabricates), and the Engine Life panel keeps its existing self-suppression on unrecognized engines — so a typo or oddball entry shows nothing, never a wrong number. ## 2026-06-28T215500Z — PASS — start-over-cancels-autofill
- Pages: /aircraft/new (Sell-your-Aircraft post form)
- What: **Clicking "Start over" on the aircraft post form now truly clears the draft, even mid-lookup — an FAA N-number lookup or AI "Prefill from notes" that resolves *after* the reset can no longer re-populate the just-cleared form or re-persist the wiped draft.** Before this, `handleLookup()` (onBlur of the N-number field) and `handleGenerate()` (AI prefill) both fetch asynchronously, then write make/model/year/etc. into the form on resolve. If the user hit **Start over** while one was in flight, `reset()` cleared the form, but the pending async fill then re-filled the fields, set a stale "Found: …" status, force-opened "More details", and dispatched `input`/`change` events that re-armed autosave → the cleared draft was written back to localStorage. Worse, clicking "Start over" *itself* blurs the registration input, which can kick off the lookup — so "Start over" appeared not to work. The fix adds a monotonic `fillTokenRef` (a `useRef`): `handleStartOver` bumps it (and clears the stale lookup/AI status so the UI reflects the cleared state) before `reset()`; `handleLookup` and `handleGenerate` each capture the token *before* their `await` and **bail out** on resolve (no field writes, no status, no auto-open, no autosave re-arm) if the token has advanced — i.e. a reset happened meanwhile. The lookup's `finally { setIsLookingUp(false) }` still runs on bail, so no stuck spinner. Pure client-side guard: no change to `useFormDraft`, the FAA route, the data model, the upload endpoints, or any copy/layout; partnership/seeker forms (no N-number lookup) are untouched. 1 file: `src/components/PostAircraftForm.tsx` (+18 lines). This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (spec + uncommitted implementation present on the staging working tree; a stale `night/start-over-cancels-autofill` branch was based on older staging and carried frozen harness edits — `run-drain.sh`/`REVIEW.md` — so it was discarded); this cycle reviewed the diff against the acceptance criteria, committed only the scoped change to a fresh `night/start-over-cancels-autofill` off current staging, re-ran the full build + typecheck + QA gate clean, and landed it.
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — closes a real data-integrity bug in the post flow: "Start over" now reliably clears the draft instead of being silently re-populated by a race, so a seller can confidently abandon a wrong/restored draft and begin a fresh listing. Data-integrity guardrail respected: removes friction (a control that didn't work) without weakening trust — no required field cut, no validation/data-model change, the normal fill path is unchanged. Rotation: last 3 cycles were P3 (airframe-utilization-read, most recent), P1 (aircraft-model-suggestions), P3 (days-on-market-vs-comps) — the most recent was Pillar 3, so Pillar 1 is due again; this is a different surface (the async-fill race on the Start-over control) than the recent model-suggestions/photo-persistence slices. Pillar 2's headline items (Google OAuth, email-only signup form) remain human-blocked behind the frozen `/auth`.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260628T214626Z-start-over-cancels-autofill.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0) and `npx next build` compiled + typechecked clean (exit 0). QA smoke (production `next start` on port 3171, `PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSERS_PATH=~/.cache/ms-playwright` after installing the project playwright's pinned chromium-headless-shell build 1228 to the writable cache — the read-only `/ms-playwright` only ships build 1223) reported HTTP **200**, **zero app-origin console errors**, and **zero horizontal overflow** at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on `/aircraft/new` — smoke exit **0**. Both passed. All acceptance criteria met.

## 2026-06-28T203500Z — PASS — airframe-utilization-read
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id] — verified on /aircraft/listing/00653d83-1a27-4d57-b3f1-fcf4a9b343f1 (1974 Cessna 172M)
- What: **Aircraft listing pages now carry a new "Airframe time" panel that turns the raw TTAF number into how hard the airframe has actually been flown over its life — average hours/year — with honest, two-sided buyer guidance.** A buyer staring at "2,700 hrs total time" on a 1974 airframe has to do the math to know that's only ~52 hrs/year; this panel does it for them (`ttaf ÷ age`) and frames what it means: a big "≈52 hrs/yr" figure, a low/typical/high band chip, a one-line headline ("Typical utilization"), and a guidance paragraph. Crucially it's **two-sided and never a score** — *low* utilization is flagged **amber** ("a thing to ask about": sitting risks dried seals/corrosion/stale fuel-system components), not a green win; *high* notes regular flying keeps systems healthy but adds cumulative wear → review the maintenance history; *typical* reads neutral. It renders right after the SMOH-based Engine Life panel and is deliberately distinct from it — airframe **total time over the aircraft's whole life**, not engine-since-overhaul. Honesty-gated by construction: the pure helper `computeAirframeUsage({ ttaf, year })` returns **null (panel self-suppresses)** when `ttaf` or `year` is missing, `ttaf <= 0`, or the model year is the current year/future (age < 1) — so it never fabricates a per-year average from absent data. No type-specific TTAF benchmarks are used (those would risk fabrication) — purely the listing's own ttaf ÷ age, explicitly labelled "a rule of thumb, not a guarantee". No schema, no new DB read (reuses `p.ttaf`/`p.year` already fetched), no network call, no new dep. 3 files: `src/lib/airframeUsage.ts` (new pure helper), `src/lib/airframeUsage.test.ts` (new, 8 unit tests), `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` (compute + `AirframeUsagePanel`). This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (impl + spec committed on `night/airframe-utilization-read` off current staging, with the unit-test file written but left uncommitted on the working tree when the prior process died before landing); this cycle committed the test, re-ran the full tests + build + typecheck + QA gate clean, and landed it.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — a genuinely proprietary read (no listing site surfaces life-average airframe utilization) synthesized from our own extracted `ttaf` spec, distinct from the SMOH Engine Life panel and the family-price Estimate. Honesty guardrail respected: self-suppresses on missing/invalid inputs (never a fabricated number), no type benchmarks, two-sided copy so low-time isn't over-sold as good. Rotation: last 3 cycles were P1 (aircraft-model-suggestions, most recent), P3 (days-on-market-vs-comps), P1 (post-photos-survive-auth) — the most recent was Pillar 1, and Pillar 2's headline items (Google OAuth, email-only signup form) remain human-blocked behind the frozen `/auth`, so Pillar 3 was the rotation-correct unblocked pillar; this is a different surface (the TTAF→hrs/yr airframe read) than the recent days-on-market relative-age slice.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260628T202415Z-airframe-utilization-read.md
- Verdict: PASS. Unit tests `node --experimental-strip-types --test src/lib/airframeUsage.test.ts` — all **8 pass** (null-gating on missing ttaf/year, ttaf ≤ 0, age < 1; low/typical/high band classification; rounding + ttaf echo). `npx tsc --noEmit` clean (exit 0) and `npx next build` compiled + typechecked clean (exit 0). QA smoke (production `next start` on port 3187, `PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSERS_PATH=~/.cache/ms-playwright`) reported HTTP **200**, **zero app-origin console errors**, and **zero horizontal overflow** at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 on the listing page — smoke exit **0**. ## 2026-06-28T193414Z — PASS — days-on-market-vs-comps
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id] — verified on /aircraft/listing/00653d83-1a27-4d57-b3f1-fcf4a9b343f1 (Cessna 172)
- What: **The "How this stacks up" panel's days-on-market signal is now relative and proprietary** — it tells the buyer how long this listing has been for sale *compared to comparable {make} {model} listings still on the market*, not just the absolute "Listed N ago". The signal keeps its absolute label (e.g. "Listed 3 days ago") and now carries a data-grounded detail line synthesized from our own `first_seen_at` across the active family, e.g. *"On the market about as long as the typical one of 66 comparable Cessna 172 listings still for sale"* (or "Listed longer than ~80% of …", or "Listed more recently than ~30% of …"). Honest by construction: it compares only against listings **still for sale** (we have no sold data, so never a survivorship-biased "how fast they sell" claim); below an honesty floor of 5 comparable listings with a known first-seen date it shows nothing new and falls back to the existing plain absolute copy; a 40–60% dead band reads "about typical" so a near-median position isn't over-claimed; and the "seller-flexibility" inference only attaches when the listing is **also absolutely stale (≥30 days)** — a fresh listing that merely out-ages an equally-fresh comp set gets neutral framing, not a fabricated negotiation cue. New pure helper `computeDaysOnMarketContext(subjectFirstSeen, compFirstSeen[], now)` (takes `now` as a param → deterministically testable, 9 worked-example unit tests). Reuses the already-fetched `getFamilyComps` set (extended to also `select`/return `first_seen_at`) so there is **no extra DB read**; the Deal Check verdict helper ignores the extra field, so its math is unchanged. The ClubHanger Estimate, Deal Check, Engine Life, and Cost-to-own panels are untouched. 4 files: `src/lib/daysOnMarket.ts` (new helper), `src/lib/daysOnMarket.test.ts` (new tests), `src/lib/aircraftForSale.ts` (`getFamilyComps` returns `first_seen_at`), `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` (compute context + enrich the signal). This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (spec + uncommitted implementation present on the working tree; the prior process died before landing); this cycle reviewed the diff against the acceptance criteria, committed it to `night/days-on-market-vs-comps` (already based on current staging), re-ran the full build + typecheck + tests + QA gate clean, and landed it.
- Goal: proprietary buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — turns days-on-market from an absolute "Listed N ago" badge into a **relative** seller-flexibility read fused from our own `first_seen_at` across the active family, distinct from the family-price ClubHanger Estimate and from anything Controller/Barnstormers/Trade-A-Plane surface. Honesty guardrail respected: honesty floor (≥5 comps), survivorship-safe framing ("still for sale", never "how fast they sell"), dead-band to avoid over-claiming, and the flexibility inference gated on real absolute age. ## 2026-06-28T145533Z — PASS — post-photos-survive-auth
- Pages: /aircraft/new
- What: **Photos uploaded on the "Sell your aircraft" form now survive the deferred-auth redirect and any page reload, instead of silently vanishing.** The post form's autosave (`useFormDraft`) already persisted every named text field across the "Sign in to Publish" round-trip, but **photos were lost**: the uploaded URLs lived only in `PartnershipPhotoUpload`'s React state (emitted as hidden `photo_url` inputs, which autosave deliberately skips). So a logged-out seller who uploaded photos — the form literally calls photos "the highest-value element of a listing" — and signed in to publish came back to an empty uploader, losing the single most valuable thing they'd added. The images are already in storage with public URLs **before** submit, so nothing needs re-uploading — only the URL references needed to persist. This cycle adds two **opt-in** props to `PartnershipPhotoUpload`: `persistKey` (mirror successfully-uploaded URLs to `localStorage` whenever they change; restore into state on mount) and `restoreGateKey` (only restore when the form's text-draft key exists — ties photo lifetime to the text draft, so photos return exactly when the draft does and are dropped once it's gone, e.g. after a successful publish clears it). `PostAircraftForm` passes `persistKey={DRAFT_KEY}:photos` + `restoreGateKey={DRAFT_KEY}`, and on "Start over" removes the photos key and bumps a React `key` to remount the uploader so its thumbnails clear too. Restored photos (URL set) flow through the existing `successPhotos` filter → hidden `photo_url` inputs → submit unchanged, so they publish with the listing. **No change to upload endpoints, storage, the submit/data model, or any copy/layout.** 2 files: `src/components/PartnershipPhotoUpload.tsx` (opt-in persist/restore), `src/components/PostAircraftForm.tsx` (wire props + Start-over clear). This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (spec + uncommitted implementation present on the staging working tree; the prior process died before landing); this cycle reviewed the diff against the acceptance criteria, committed it to a fresh `night/post-photos-survive-auth` off current staging, re-ran the full build + typecheck + QA gate clean, and landed it.
- Goal: frictionless-posting pillar (Pillar 1) — closes the last data-loss in the post flow: a logged-out seller's photos now survive the deferred-auth gate, pairing the existing text-draft autosave with photo persistence so the whole half-filled listing comes back intact ("post first, sign in to publish, draft intact"). Data-integrity guardrail respected: persistence is opt-in (partnership/seeker forms pass neither prop → unchanged), gated on the text-draft key so no stale photos leak into a fresh listing after publish, and the data model / endpoints are untouched. Rotation: last 3 cycles were P2 (soft-save-keep-intent, most recent), P3 (estimate-price-bar), P1 (draft-start-over) — the most recent was P2, so Pillar 1 is due again; this is a different surface (photo persistence in the uploader) than that earlier draft-lifecycle/Start-over slice, and it directly completes the `draft-start-over` lineage by extending autosave to the one field it never covered.

The subject's own price is excluded from the comp set (so it can fall at/below `low` or at/above `high`), so the marker is **clamped to [0,100]%** — consistent with the existing "priced below/above all of them" copy. A `role="img"` + `aria-label` describes the position for screen readers. 1 file: `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` (`EstimatePanel` only). Note: the value-axis marker (≈45% of the way up $5k–$435k) and the rank-based percentile (88%) legitimately differ because the comp prices are right-skewed (a few very expensive comps stretch the high to $435k); the bar is explicitly a price-value axis (low–median–high), so positioning the marker by value is the consistent, honest choice and matches its own labels.

## 2026-06-28T140214Z — PASS — draft-start-over
- Pages: /aircraft/new, /partnerships/new, /partnerships/seeking/new
- What: **Every "Post a…" form now has a one-click, guarded "Start over" control so a returning user whose autosaved draft was restored can clear it and begin a fresh listing without wiping each field by hand.** Autosave + restore already worked (`useFormDraft`), but a *restored* draft was a dead end if it was the wrong one (e.g. the user wants to list a different aircraft): they had to manually empty every field. This cycle adds a `reset()` callback to `useFormDraft` — it clears the debounce timer, drops the failed-submit snapshot, removes the localStorage draft key, calls native `form.reset()` (so the uncontrolled fields empty back to their HTML defaults — note `reset()` fires no input/change, so autosave does **not** re-arm), and sets `status` back to `idle`. All three Post forms (`PostAircraftForm`, `PostPartnershipForm`, `PostSeekerListingForm`) render a subtle `type="button"` "Start over" link beside the draft indicator, shown **only when a draft exists** (`status === 'saved' || 'restored'`) and hidden otherwise; clicking it `window.confirm()`s before wiping (guard against accidental data loss). 4 files: `src/components/useFormDraft.ts` (+`reset()`), and the three form components (wire `reset` → guarded `handleStartOver`, render the control). This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (spec + uncommitted implementation present on `night/draft-start-over`; the prior process died before landing); this cycle reviewed the diff against acceptance criteria, committed it, re-ran the full build + typecheck + QA gate clean, and landed it.

Pairs with the existing autosave/restore. Data-integrity guardrail respected: the control is confirm-gated, `type="button"` (never submits), and doesn't touch what fields are required or how the action saves. So a shopper sees the full "~$X to buy in + ~$Y/mo to run it" picture at a glance. Pure arithmetic on the real `asking_price` (`Math.round(price / shares)`) — no fabrication; the caveat copy clearly frames the buy-in as the asking price split evenly, "the real figure is negotiated." 3 files: `src/lib/calculators.ts` (added `buyInPerShare` to `ShareCostRow` + `estimateShareCosts`), `src/components/ShareCostPanel.tsx` (featured card line + table column + caveat copy), `src/lib/calculators.test.ts` (unit assertion). ## 2026-06-28T124716Z — PASS — nav-signin-filter-intent
- Pages: global nav (every page) — verified on /aircraft?make=Cessna, /partnerships, /
- What: **The global-nav "Sign in" link now preserves a logged-out visitor's FULL current URL — including active query-string filters — across the auth round trip**, so a shopper mid-filter (e.g. `/aircraft?make=Cessna`) returns to their *exact filtered view* after signing in instead of the bare pathname. The prior `nav-signin-intent-next` cycle wired the nav Sign-in button to preserve the **pathname** via `?next=`, but explicitly left query-string filters out of scope because doing it with `useSearchParams` would force this layout-level nav (and therefore every page) into client/dynamic rendering and risk a CWV regression. Since `Nav` is already `'use client'`, this cycle reads `window.location.pathname + window.location.search` **at click time** in a new `handleSignInClick` handler: on a plain left-click it `preventDefault()`s, closes the mobile menu, and `router.push`es `/auth?next=<encoded full URL>` (or bare `/auth` on the homepage); modified clicks (cmd/ctrl/shift/alt or non-primary button) fall through to the native pathname-only `href={signInHref}` so new-tab / no-JS / SSR all still work. The handler is wired as `onClick` on both the desktop and mobile Sign-in `<Link>`s. **No `useSearchParams` is introduced — the nav/layout rendering mode is unchanged.** 1 file: `src/components/Nav.tsx`.
- Goal: frictionless signup/auth pillar (Pillar 2). Friction removed: closes the last intent-drop in the most-clicked auth entry point — the global nav Sign-in button now carries the shopper's *filters*, not just their page, across auth, so a curated browse (make / price / hours filters) survives the sign-in gate. Honesty/guardrail: pathname-only `href` is retained as the no-JS/new-tab fallback (graceful degradation), and the `?next=` redirect target is still the frozen `/auth` page (untouched). Rotation: last 3 cycles were P3 (deal-score-signal-tally), then P1 (partnership-post-photos-visible — most recent), with P2 (nav-signin-intent-next) before them; the two most recent were P1 then P3, so Pillar 2 is due again — and this is a different surface/slice (query-filter preservation) than that earlier pathname-only nav slice, directly completing the gap it left.

## 2026-06-28T101832Z — PASS — save-search-intent-restore
- Pages: /aircraft, /partnerships, /partnerships/seeking
- What: **A logged-out visitor's "Save this search" now completes automatically after they sign in, instead of being silently dropped.** Before, clicking "Save this search" while signed out sent the user to `/auth?next=<filtered page>` and, on return, just re-rendered the button — they had to find and click it a second time, and many didn't. Now `SaveSearchButton` appends a `saveSearch=1` intent marker to the `next=` URL (mirroring the `?contact=1` auto-open idiom the message buttons already use). When the user lands back on the filtered page authenticated, a `useEffect` fires the save exactly once — ref-guarded so a re-render can't double-save, and the marker is stripped from the URL via `window.history.replaceState` so a page reload won't re-fire it. The saved query and its auto-generated name are computed from the active filters **minus** the marker, so `saveSearch=1` never leaks into the stored search. The signed-in direct-save path and the button's self-suppression when there are no active filters are unchanged. 1 file: `src/components/SaveSearchButton.tsx`.
- Goal: frictionless signup/auth pillar (Pillar 2) — preserves user intent across the auth round trip so the value action the user already committed to isn't lost at the gate. Friction removed: eliminates the second click (and the silent intent-drop) after sign-in for save-search, completing the `?next=`-intent-preservation pattern for the third value action (after contact and save-listing). Rotation: last 3 cycles were Pillar 1 (photo-upload-persistent-drop-paste), Pillar 3 (estimate-price-range), Pillar 2 (desktop-contact-intent-restore) — Pillar 2 was due again and this is a different value action (save-search) than the contact slice.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260628T101832Z-save-search-intent-restore.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` compiled + typechecked clean (exit 0). QA smoke (`next start` production build on port 3000, `PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSERS_PATH=/tmp/pw-browsers` — the system `/ms-playwright` browser binaries were missing/incomplete and that dir is root-owned, so chromium was installed to a writable path) exit **0** — 6/6 across `/aircraft`, `/partnerships`, `/partnerships/seeking` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 (HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow). Non-visual/behavioral cycle (logic-only; the button's rendered appearance is unchanged and it self-suppresses on the bare smoke paths that carry no filters), so the smoke gate is the gate — screenshots saved for the audit trail only. Hooks-order verified by code review: all hooks run before the `if (!cleanParams) return null` early return; marker-strip + ref guard ensure the auto-save fires at most once.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/save-search-intent-restore/

## 2026-06-28T094346Z — PASS — photo-upload-persistent-drop-paste
- Pages: /aircraft/new, /partnerships/new
- What: **The photo uploader on both post forms is now a persistent drop target and accepts clipboard paste.** `PartnershipPhotoUpload` (shared by `/aircraft/new` and `/partnerships/new`) previously rendered its drag-drop zone ONLY while `photos.length === 0`, so after the first photo landed the advertised fastest path — drag-drop — silently stopped working and the only way to add photos 2–5 was the small "+" tile → file browser. This cycle (1) lifts `onDragOver`/`onDragLeave`/`onDrop` from the empty-state zone to the **outer container**, so a drop anywhere on the component adds files whether or not photos already exist, with a subtle `ring-2 ring-sky-300` highlight shown once photos are present (the empty state keeps its big dashed zone); and (2) adds a document-level `paste` listener (mounted via `useEffect`, removed on unmount) that adds any image files from the clipboard — **guarded** to bail when an INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT/contentEditable is focused, so it never hijacks the "Prefill from your notes" AI textarea or any field. `addFiles` is already `useCallback`-memoized so the listener dep is stable. Respects `MAX_PHOTOS` (5) and the existing per-file slicing. Empty-state copy now reads "Drag or paste photos here, or browse"; the with-photos helper reads "{n}/{m} uploaded · drag, paste, or tap + to add more (up to 5)". 1 file: `src/components/PartnershipPhotoUpload.tsx`. No change to upload endpoints, storage, MAX_PHOTOS, accepted types, or the 5 MB limit.

Added `low`/`high` to the `ClubHangerEstimate` interface and to BOTH return branches (the `around` dead-band branch and the `below`/`above` branch). `EstimatePanel` renders the range in the existing caption and falls back to the prior median-only sentence when `low == high` (degenerate single-value spread → no "$X–$X" non-range). 3 files: `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.ts` (interface + both returns), `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` (EstimatePanel caption), `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.test.ts` (assert low/high on the below-market case).

## 2026-06-28T084133Z — PASS — nnumber-make-fallback
- Pages: /aircraft/new, /partnerships/new
- What: **The N-number lookup and AI autofill now correctly fill the required Make field for aircraft whose make isn't one of the 8 dropdown presets (Maule, Aviat, Bellanca, Aeronca, American Champion, Socata, …) instead of silently leaving it blank.** The post forms have a fixed `MAKES` dropdown of 8 makes + "Other"; `matchMake` in `/api/faa-lookup` mapped the FAA manufacturer name to one of those 8 and returned `''` for anything else. The form then did `makeSelect.value = data.make` — but setting a `<select>` to a value with no matching `<option>` is a no-op, so Make (a **required** field) stayed blank even though the status read "Found: 1978 Maule M-5" and Model/Year filled in. The owner of any non-preset make hit a confusing blank-required-field / validation error. The AI prefill path had the same flaw (the LLM can return any make string). Fix: (1) `matchMake` now falls back to the registry's own make name in clean Title Case via a new `cleanMakeName` helper (e.g. "MAULE" → "Maule", "AVIAT AIRCRAFT INC" → "Aviat Aircraft" — title-cased + trailing corporate suffix dropped) instead of `''`; it never invents a name and still returns `''` only when the FAA gave no make at all. (2) Both forms gained a `fillMakeSelect` helper that injects an `<option>` (before "Other") for makes not already in the dropdown, then selects it — so the real make is stored (better data than blank/"Other") and the required field fills. Canonical makes (Cessna, Piper, …) still select their existing option with no duplicate injected. 3 files: `src/app/api/faa-lookup/route.ts` (add `cleanMakeName`; `matchMake` fallback + empty-input guard); `src/components/PostAircraftForm.tsx` and `src/components/PostPartnershipForm.tsx` (add `fillMakeSelect`; wire it into both the N-number-lookup and AI-prefill paths).
- Goal: posting pillar (Pillar 1) — fixes a posting-flow bug in a recently-shipped activation feature (the `nnumber-autofill` / `partnership-nnumber-autofill` lookups). It both removes friction (no more blank required Make for non-preset owners) AND improves data integrity (the true make is stored, satisfying the GOAL guardrail against trading integrity for less friction). Rotation: last cycle was Pillar 3 (partnership-comp-magnitude); this returns to Pillar 1. This was an in-flight branch from a prior cycle (implementation + spec + screenshots present but never landed — likely the prior process died after a transient cold-start QA failure); this cycle re-ran the full build+QA gate clean and landed it.

## 2026-06-27T140520Z — PASS — lazy-name-save
- Pages: /partnerships/new, /partnerships/seeking/new
- What: **Magic-link users who post a listing now have their name remembered for future post forms.** Previously, magic-link sign-in users had no `full_name` in their Supabase user metadata (Google OAuth populates this automatically; magic link does not), so the contact-prefill feature left the "Your Name" field blank on every post form visit — they had to retype it each time. Now, when a magic-link user submits a partnership or seeking listing with a non-empty contact name, the `createPartnership` / `createSeekerListing` server actions silently call `supabase.auth.updateUser({data:{full_name:...}})` to persist the name. On their next visit, the existing contact-prefill logic picks it up and pre-fills the field automatically. Google OAuth users and users who already have a display name are unaffected. Also adds a one-line hint under the name field ("We'll save your name for future listings.") when the user is logged in but has no saved name yet. 3 files changed: `src/app/actions.ts` (name-save logic in `createPartnership` + `createSeekerListing`); `src/components/PostPartnershipForm.tsx` (hint text); `src/components/PostSeekerListingForm.tsx` (conditional hint replacing static hint).
- Goal: signup pillar (Pillar 2) — closes the display-name gap for magic-link users in the post flow. The contact-prefill cycle (`contact-prefill`) shipped name pre-fill for Google OAuth users; this cycle extends it to magic-link users without any new UI — just remembering what the user already typed. Friction removed: magic-link users type their name once, not every post. Rotating to Pillar 2 (last cycle was Pillar 1 — nnumber-autofill).

## 2026-06-27T131252Z — PASS — homerails-deal-chips

- What: **Homepage curated rails ("Browse curated collections") now show year+hours-controlled "Good deal" (emerald) or "Priced high" (amber) chips on aircraft cards** — the last aircraft surface without deal verdict chips. Previously, AircraftRailCards in HomeRails passed no `compVerdict`, so homepage rail cards showed no deal signal. Now HomeRails batch-fetches comps for every unique make+model family across all rail listings in one parallel `Promise.all` (one Supabase read per unique family, not per listing), computes `clubHangerDealVerdict` per listing self-excluding from its own comp set, and passes `compVerdict` to each `AircraftRailCard`. The `AircraftRailCard` component already supported `compVerdict` (added in `deal-verdict-rail-cards`); only HomeRails needed updating. Self-suppression is unchanged — listings with missing year/ttaf or thin comp sets (<4 within ±5 yr / similar hours) show no chip. 1 file changed: `src/components/HomeRails.tsx` (3 new imports; `FamilyKey`/`FamilySpec`/`BatchComp` types; early-return guard moved above comp-fetch; batch family-collect + `Promise.all` comp fetch + verdict-compute block; `compVerdict={verdicts.get(p.id)}` on each `AircraftRailCard`).

Previous two cycles were Pillar 3 (`deal-verdict-rail-cards`) and Pillar 2 (`alert-weekly-digest`); Pillar 1 P1 queue is exhausted; this completes the natural Pillar 3 rollout.

## 2026-06-27T125858Z — PASS — deal-verdict-rail-cards
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **The "Similar aircraft for sale" rail on listing detail pages now shows the same year+hours-controlled "Good deal" / "Priced high" chips as browse cards**, instead of the less-accurate whole-family estimate it used before. Previously, the rail used `clubHangerEstimate` (comparing against the entire make+model family, no year or hours control) — a 1970 Cessna 172 listed below the family median (which includes modern avionics-equipped 172s) would falsely show "Good deal." Now the rail uses `clubHangerDealVerdict` (same as browse cards), which only awards a chip when ≥4 comps fall within ±5 years AND similar hours of the subject listing. Listings without year or ttaf show no chip. New `getFamilyCompsForBatch` helper in `aircraftForSale.ts` fetches id+price+year+ttaf for all active family comps in one query; each listing self-excludes from its own comp set in JS — no N+1 query problem. 2 files changed: `src/lib/aircraftForSale.ts` (new `getFamilyCompsForBatch`); `src/components/SimilarAircraft.tsx` (replace `getFamilyAskingPrices` + `clubHangerEstimate` with `getFamilyCompsForBatch` + `clubHangerDealVerdict`; self-exclusion by id; updated JSDoc).
- Goal: buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — closes the deal-verdict chip rollout across all three aircraft discovery surfaces: detail page (already had it via EstimatePanel + DealScorePanel) → browse cards (shipped in `deal-verdict-browse-chips`) → Similar aircraft rail (this cycle). Buyers looking at a listing and scrolling to "Similar aircraft" now see the same honest, year+hours-controlled verdict on every comparable card, without needing to click in. Previous two cycles were Pillar 2 (alert-weekly-digest) and Pillar 1 (parts-wanted-filter); rotating to Pillar 3.

## 2026-06-27T124751Z — PASS — alert-weekly-digest
- Pages: /api/cron/alert-digest (new internal cron endpoint; no user-facing page changes)
- What: **The email-alert subscriber loop is now complete.** Confirmed subscribers now receive a weekly digest when new matching listings exist. A new `GET /api/cron/alert-digest` route (called daily at 08:00 UTC by Vercel cron) queries all `status='confirmed'` alerts whose `last_digest_at` is older than 7 days (or null). For each, it parses the `source_path` (e.g. `/aircraft/cessna/172`, `/partnerships/near/khwd`, `/aircraft/for-sale/california`) into typed filter params, counts new aircraft or partnership listings since the subscriber's last digest, and if the count is > 0 sends a "N new {context} listings" email via `sendEmail` (no-ops safely if `RESEND_API_KEY` is absent) and stamps `last_digest_at`. Zero matches → alert skipped, `last_digest_at` unchanged (re-checked tomorrow). New `vercel.json` wires the daily cron schedule. New `buildAlertDigestEmail` in `src/lib/email.ts`. 3 files changed/created: `src/app/api/cron/alert-digest/route.ts` (new, 251 lines); `src/lib/email.ts` (add `buildAlertDigestEmail`); `vercel.json` (new cron config). **Human action needed:** set `CRON_SECRET` in the Vercel dashboard (Dashboard → Project → Settings → Environment Variables) and pass it in the Authorization header `Bearer $CRON_SECRET`; without it the route is unprotected (warning logged, not error). Also ensure `RESEND_API_KEY` and sender domain are verified in Resend before real emails go out.
- Goal: signup pillar (Pillar 2 adjacent) — completes the email-alert retention loop. Subscribers who opted in for Cessna 172 alerts (or any make/model/state/airport alerts) have been getting confirmation emails since slice 2 shipped, but NO follow-up when new listings appeared. This is the missing link: the digest that makes the subscription valuable. Previous two cycles were Pillar 1 (parts-wanted-filter) and Pillar 3 (deal-verdict-browse-chips). Pillar 2 P1 items are frozen on auth files; this is the highest-value doable Pillar 2 / retention item in the backlog ("Build slices 2-3 NOW").

## 2026-06-27T122500Z — PASS — deal-verdict-browse-chips
- Pages: /aircraft
- What: **Aircraft browse cards now show a year- and hours-controlled "Good deal" or "Priced high" chip in the badge row.** The existing "~X% below/above average" CompPill compared a listing's price to the whole make+model family — a 1970 Cessna 172 would look "below market" simply because 2020s are in the same family. The new chip (`clubHangerDealVerdict`) first narrows the comp set to listings within ±5 years and similar total time (±1 000 hrs or 35%), then calls "Good deal" (emerald) or "Priced high" (amber). "Fair price" is suppressed. When the controlled comp set is thin (missing year/ttaf, or fewer than 4 matches), the card falls back to the existing CompPill — no regression. On the first browse page, 4 "Good deal" and 2 "Priced high" chips appeared; remaining cards showed CompPill or no price chip. 2 files changed: `AircraftSaleList.tsx` (new `fetchFamilyCompMap` fetching `id, year, ttaf` alongside prices; `clubHangerDealVerdict` computed per listing; `comp` nulled when deal verdict is available); `AircraftSaleCard.tsx` (new `dealVerdict` prop + `DealCheckChip` component; DealCheckChip renders instead of CompPill when verdict is present).
- Goal: buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — surfaces the Deal Check verdict (already shipping on detail pages) at browse discovery layer. Buyers previously had to click into every listing to see the year+hours-controlled verdict; now they can spot genuine bargains and avoid overpriced listings at a glance on the browse card. Completes the "remaining" slice noted in the `clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict` BACKLOG entry. Previous cycle was Pillar 2 (defer-partnership-search-gate); rotating to Pillar 3.

## 2026-06-27T06:18:14Z — PASS — deal-score-panel
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Aircraft listing pages now show a "How this stacks up" panel that synthesizes up to four buyer-relevant signals into one scannable card.** The panel appears in the main content column between the Specifications grid and the Engine Life panel. It shows: (1) price positioning — "Good deal / Fair price / Priced high" from the Deal Check (year+hours-controlled comps) or, when that's unavailable, the family-wide ClubHanger Estimate; (2) days on market — derived from `first_seen_at`, labelled "Fresh to market" (≤3 days), "Listed N days/months ago" (up to 30 days), or "Listed N months ago — seller may have flexibility" (≥90 days); (3) price history — "Price reduced $X — a seller motivation signal" or "Price increased $X" when a real recorded change exists; (4) spec completeness — "Well documented / N/5 key specs" based on presence of year, TTAF, SMOH, engine type, and registration. Each row has a colored dot (emerald for positive, slate for neutral, amber for negative), a bold label, and a plain-language detail line explaining what the signal means for a buyer. The panel self-suppresses when fewer than 2 signals are actionable. No new DB queries — everything derives from data already fetched on the page. 1 file changed (197 lines, `computeDealSignals` helper + `DealScorePanel` component).
- Goal: buyer-analysis pillar (Pillar 3) — Deal Score panel. Previous two activation cycles were Pillar 1 (partnership-post-prefill-all-fields) and Pillar 2 (partnership-post-deferred-gate); rotating back to Pillar 3. Friction removed: buyers previously had to read four separate panels (ClubHanger Estimate, Engine Life, Price History, Listing Completeness) to understand the story; now one card at the top of the content column gives the synthesis with transparent reasons — no black-box score.

## 2026-06-26T124800Z — PASS — aircraft-airport-filter
- Pages: /aircraft
- What: **Buyers can now filter aircraft for sale by airport.** A new "Near airport (ICAO)" text input appears in the "More filters" section on `/aircraft`. Server-side: the ICAO is looked up against the `airports` table, resolved to a US state, then applied as `.eq('state', …)` on the listing query. Falls back gracefully when the code isn't in our table (shows all listings, no crash). 3 files: `AircraftSaleList.tsx` (Filters interface + fetchAircraftPage airport→state lookup), `AircraftSaleFilters.tsx` (Near airport input + SECONDARY_KEYS), `ActiveFilterChips.tsx` (Near KSFO chip).

One-click, accurate listings from public data; no owner names/emails are shown (FAA has none). 2 files: new `/api/faa-lookup` route (parses the FAA inquiry HTML for Mfr/Model/Year/registrant type, fails soft to HTTP 200 on any error — never 500); `PostAircraftForm.tsx` gains the Look-up button + handler (same DOM-fill pattern as the existing AI-draft autofill).

## 2026-06-25T101126Z — PASS — message-notify-throttle
- Pages: /messages, /messages/[threadId]
- What: **On-site message email notifications are now throttled to at most one per thread per hour.** Previously, every message sent in a conversation triggered an email to the recipient — a rapid back-and-forth exchange could produce an inbox-flooding burst of "You have a new message" emails. Now `notifyMessageRecipient` checks an in-process `MESSAGE_NOTIFY_LAST` Map before sending: if an email was already delivered for this thread within the past hour, it skips silently and the message still saves. The first message after any 1-hour quiet window still fires normally. Same fire-and-forget pattern as before; no user-visible change on a single-message thread.
- Goal: feature quality / defensive UX — `[want]` lane (last 3 non-bug cycles: seeking-drive-time [want], messaging-new-message-email [want], model-curate-cessna-421 [goal] — not all 3 [want], so [want] owed per 3:1 policy). Explicitly queued in messaging-new-message-email CHANGELOG "Next" notes. Pageviews at orient: 374 last 7d (PostHog secondary; GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING). Pure server-side change: 1 file (`src/app/actions.ts`), ~17 lines added — a module-level `Map<string, number>` (threadId → last-sent timestamp) + one guard block at the top of `notifyMessageRecipient`. Same in-process pattern as `AI_DRAFT_CALLS`; effective for current traffic / warm-instance reuse; swap for Redis/KV if traffic grows significantly.
- Goal-lane: [want]
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260625T101126Z-message-notify-throttle.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` compiled clean (exit 0, no TypeScript errors). QA smoke (`next start` production build on port 3020, NOT dev) — exit 0 on `/messages`, `/partnerships/seeking`, `/aircraft` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 (6/6 — HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow). Non-visual cycle (server-side logic only, no UI change) — screenshots saved as audit trail, not read.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/message-notify-throttle/
- Next: (1) Rate limit is in-process — if Vercel cold-starts or traffic spikes, some threads may get a second notification before the Map warms up; swap for a Supabase-backed `last_notified_at` column on `threads` for true durability (additive schema, human DDL). (2) The interval is 1 hour — consider whether 30 min or per-day is the right cadence once the feature is live and the human has set RESEND_API_KEY. (3) The alerts double-opt-in confirmation email (slice 2 of email alerts) is ready to queue next.

Fire-and-forget via `void` — no latency added to the message send. ## 2026-06-24T12:50Z — PASS — guide-flying-club-vs-co-ownership
- Pages: /guides/flying-club-vs-co-ownership, /guides
- What: **New plain-English guide: "Flying Club vs. Aircraft Co-Ownership."** It answers a real question pilots weigh when they want to fly affordably — join a flying club (pay to belong and rent the club's planes) or buy a share of one aircraft with a few partners. The guide compares the two side by side: what you pay and what you build (equity), fleet access vs. one shared plane, who controls the schedule and maintenance, how easy each is to get into and out of, who each suits, and how to decide — with the same honest, "this is not legal/tax/financial advice" framing as the sibling guides. It now shows as a card on the Guides hub and links out to the related guides, the cost calculator, and partnerships.
- Goal: SEO content depth / INDEXING stage — `[goal]` lane (last non-bug cycle `saved-search-inline-rename` pulled `[want]` → alternated to `[goal]`). ## 2026-06-24T10:21Z — PASS — clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each internal for-sale aircraft page can now show an honest "Good deal / Fair price / Priced high" verdict** — the endorsement-style read the ClubHanger Estimate has been building toward. The existing estimate already said whether a plane is priced **above or below the whole make+model family**, but that alone isn't a fair verdict (a 1976 Cessna 172 is "below" the family median simply because it's old, not because it's a bargain). The new **"Deal check"** line, shown right under the family comparison, fixes that by comparing the asking price **only against similar-year (±5 years) and similar-hours listings of the same make and model** — controlling for the two biggest things that move an airplane's price. So on a real example this run, a **1976 Cessna 172M at $120k** reads **"Below market"** vs all 172s but **"Fair price"** once you look only at other mid-1970s, comparable-hours 172s — a genuinely useful, honest distinction. It states the comp basis and count in plain English ("compared with 4 … listings within ±5 years and comparable total time, median $X"), and shows **nothing at all** when the listing lacks a year or total time, or when there aren't at least 4 truly comparable listings — no made-up verdict on thin data.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow-Zestimate parity, the brand differentiator) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `compare-pairs-expansion` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS → no blocker → [want] owed per the 1:1). This is the remaining slice of the flagship **[P1][want] "ClubHanger Estimate — fair-value pricing"** item, whose backlog note explicitly gated the value verdict on *"once comps are narrowed to year-band + hours (then a value judgement is honest)"* — delivered exactly, and **additively** (the existing whole-family descriptive estimate is untouched). A product win the pageview metric can't see tonight. Honesty-rule-clean: a value judgement is published only on a year+hours-controlled comp set of ≥4, with a ±5% dead band reading "Fair price", whole-dollar/percent only, and an explicit "estimate, not an appraisal" framing; self-suppresses on thin/missing data. Scoreboard at orient: 325 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).
- Spec: nightshift/specs/2026-06-24T10-14-40Z-clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict.md
- Verdict: PASS. Four files, additive. `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.ts` — new pure, import-free `clubHangerDealVerdict(subject, comps)` + exported bands (`MIN_DEAL_COMPS=4`, `DEAL_YEAR_BAND=5`, hours band = max(1,000 hrs, ±35%), `DEAL_DEAD_BAND=5%`); returns null unless the subject has a real price+year+ttaf AND ≥4 comps fall inside both bands. `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.test.ts` — 7 new worked-example tests (good/fair/high, out-of-band exclusion, relative hours band, null on missing year/ttaf, null on thin narrowed set); **12/12 pass** via `node --experimental-strip-types --test`. `src/lib/aircraftForSale.ts` — read-only `getFamilyComps()` (selects year+ttaf, `.neq('id', self)`, same family filter as `getFamilyAskingPrices`, fails soft to []); the two family reads run concurrently via `Promise.all`. `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` — additive `DealCheck` sub-block inside `EstimatePanel` (new optional `deal` prop); existing family-median path unchanged. NO schema/DB change, NO new dependency, NO new route. `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 24.4s"); `tsc --noEmit` clean in all touched source files (only the pre-existing `.test.ts` TS5097 import-extension baseline remains). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start -p 3100`, NOT dev): qa-smoke exit 0 on a real `/aircraft/listing/[id]` (the 1976 C172M above) + `/aircraft` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 (4/4 — HTTP 200, **zero** app-origin console errors, **zero** horizontal overflow). Read the screenshots: the layered panel renders cleanly at both viewports (family "Below market" then the bordered "Deal check / Fair price" sub-section), single-column on mobile, no overflow. Verified across many SR22/172 listings that the verdict self-suppresses correctly when a listing has no year and/or too few similar-year+hours comps — the honesty floor is doing real work.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict/

## 2026-06-23T08:35Z — PASS — alerts-double-opt-in
- Pages: /alerts/status, /aircraft (the alert-signup box), plus two new backend routes (/api/alerts/confirm, /api/alerts/unsubscribe)
- What: **Email alerts now use a proper double-opt-in flow — sign up, get a confirmation email, click to confirm, and a working one-click unsubscribe.** Until now, when a visitor entered their email to get alerts for new listings (the "Get alerts for new Cessna 172 listings" box on the for-sale pages), the address was just stored as "pending" with no way to confirm it or opt back out — so we could never actually, responsibly send a single alert. This cycle wires the real flow: a new signup now triggers a confirmation email with a "Confirm my alerts" button and an unsubscribe link; clicking confirm flips the subscription to **confirmed**, clicking unsubscribe flips it to **unsubscribed**, and both land on a clean branded ClubHanger page telling the visitor what happened. The signup box's success message now says "Almost there — check your inbox" instead of implying they're already subscribed. **Nothing actually sends yet** — the email layer is built to send via Resend the moment the human drops in a `RESEND_API_KEY`, and until then every send is a safe logged no-op (so this ships with zero risk of mailing anyone prematurely).
- Goal: feature depth / conversion infrastructure — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `airport-og-card-parity` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). This is **slice 2** of the top **[P1][want] "Email alerts capture"** item; the backlog explicitly says "Build slices 2-3 NOW, gated behind `RESEND_API_KEY` — do NOT block on the key... no-op + log when it's absent," and the double-opt-in schema (`confirm_token`/`confirmed_at`/`unsubscribe_token`) is already migrated. Slice 1 (capture UI + pending insert) shipped earlier. A list-building / conversion win the pageview metric can't see tonight; it's the prerequisite that makes the list legally sendable (CAN-SPAM/GDPR confirmed opt-in + one-click unsubscribe). Honesty-rule-clean: no fabricated content, no actual sends without a key, soft-fails on bad tokens. Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

- Verdict: PASS. New `src/lib/email.ts` — `sendEmail()` POSTs to the Resend API when `RESEND_API_KEY` is set, else logs `[email:noop]` and returns `{sent:false}` (verified the key is ABSENT in this env, so the no-op path is what runs); plus `buildAlertConfirmEmail()` (HTML + text, escaped). `subscribeToAlerts` now mints `confirm_token`+`unsubscribe_token` in-app (so it can build the email links without reading the row back — anon has no SELECT on `alerts` by design), inserts them, and on a genuinely NEW row sends the confirmation (skips it on a 23505 dedupe so a resubmit can't spam an address). ## 2026-06-23T08:01Z — PASS — clubhanger-estimate-detail
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each for-sale aircraft's own page now shows a "ClubHanger Estimate" — how its asking price compares to the going rate for the same make+model.** Right under the price, a new panel reads the median asking price of every *other* active, priced listing of the same make+model family and tells the buyer, in one line, whether this plane is asking **Below market / Around market / Above market** — e.g. "Above market · Asking $49,900 (40%) above the median Cessna 172 listing", with the comp count and median shown ("Based on the median asking price of N other Cessna 172 listings for sale now") and a link to see the whole family. It's deliberately a **descriptive market comparison, not a "good deal" endorsement**: the comp set is the entire make+model family, so a big gap usually reflects year/hours/avionics rather than a bargain — the panel says exactly that ("actual value also depends on year, hours, and avionics. An estimate, not an appraisal or an offer"). The block only appears when the listing has a real price AND there are at least 4 other priced same-family comps; on no-price, unknown-family, or thin-data listings it simply doesn't render.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow "Zestimate" analog) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `home-rail-cards-internal-link` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). A flagship product differentiator the pageview metric can't see tonight; it also adds buyer-useful depth + an internal family link to the just-indexed detail family. Honesty-rule-clean: real same-family asking prices only, whole-number $/%, a ±5% "Around market" dead band, a hard ≥4-comp floor, and a prominent caveat — no fabricated value, and crucially NOT framed as an endorsement (the backlog's "good deal" score is deferred until year-band/hours comps exist; see Next).
